<p><b>Terrence LeVarr Thornton</b> (born May 13, 1977),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> better known by his stage name <b>Pusha T</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> is an American rapper, songwriter, and record executive. He rose to prominence as one-half of the Virginia-based hip hop duo <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a>, which was mainly active from 1994 to 2010, alongside his older brother <a href="/wiki/No_Malice" title="No Malice">No Malice</a>. As Clipse, the two released three studio albums upon signing to <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Star_Trak_Entertainment" title="Star Trak Entertainment">Star Trak Entertainment</a>; the albums spawned hit singles including "<a href="/wiki/Grindin%27" title="Grindin&#39;">Grindin'</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/When_the_Last_Time" title="When the Last Time">When the Last Time</a>" (both 2002).
</p><p>In September 2010, Pusha T signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> imprint, under the aegis of <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>. Later that year, he was featured on West's single "<a href="/wiki/Runaway_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Runaway (Kanye West song)">Runaway</a>," which peaked at number 12 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. In 2011, he released his first solo project, the mixtape <i>Fear of God</i>, which was followed up with his debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is_My_Name" title="My Name Is My Name">My Name Is My Name</a></i>, released in 2013. In November 2015, West appointed Pusha T to take over his role as president of GOOD Music, where he remained one of its flagship artists until parting ways with the label in 2022. 
</p><p>Pusha T has released a further three solo albums: <i><a href="/wiki/King_Push_%E2%80%93_Darkest_Before_Dawn:_The_Prelude" title="King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude">King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude</a></i> (2015), <i><a href="/wiki/Daytona_(album)" title="Daytona (album)">Daytona</a></i> (2018), and <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Almost_Dry" title="It&#39;s Almost Dry">It's Almost Dry</a></i> (2022), all receiving widespread critical acclaim; the latter was Pusha T's first number one debut on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Pusha T was born Terrence LeVarr Thornton on May 13, 1977, in the <a href="/wiki/Bronx" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronx">Bronx</a> borough of New York City, though the family soon relocated to <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach, Virginia</a>, where he and his brother, <a href="/wiki/No_Malice" title="No Malice">Gene Thornton</a>, grew up.<sup id="cite_ref-vv_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vv-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As teenagers, the brothers both sold drugs, with Gene eventually being kicked out of their parents' house after they discovered what he was doing.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, alongside his brother, the two began to pursue a career in <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, forming a group known as <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a>. His older brother Gene was known for most of the group's duration as Malice (the two were originally known as <b>Terrar</b> and Malicious, respectively, and in 2012 Gene changed his stage name to <a href="/wiki/No_Malice" title="No Malice">No Malice</a>, following a <a href="/wiki/Conversion_to_Christianity" title="Conversion to Christianity">conversion to Christianity</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1993.E2.80.932010:_Clipse"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1993–2010:_Clipse">1993–2010: Clipse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1993–2010: Clipse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg/220px-Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg/330px-Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg/440px-Pusha_T_in_Cambridge_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1063" /></a><figcaption>Pusha T performing at <a href="/wiki/The_Middle_East_(nightclub)" title="The Middle East (nightclub)">The Middle East</a> in 2007 as part of <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Shortly after forming Clipse, the brothers were introduced to record producer and fellow Virginian <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, who helped them secure a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra Records</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Terrence initially took the stage name <b>Terrar</b>. After being signed to Elektra, they began working on their debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Audio_Footage" title="Exclusive Audio Footage">Exclusive Audio Footage</a></i>. After recording the entire album, they released one single, "The Funeral", which was commercially unsuccessful and eventually led to the release of the album being cancelled and Clipse being dropped from the label shortly after. After being dropped, Terrar changed his name to <b>Pusha T</b>, and despite not being signed to a major label, he made numerous appearances on other artists' songs, appearing on <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a>' 1999 single "<a href="/wiki/Good_Stuff_(Kelis_song)" title="Good Stuff (Kelis song)">Good Stuff</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Nivea_(singer)" title="Nivea (singer)">Nivea</a>'s 2001 single "<a href="/wiki/Run_Away_(I_Wanna_Be_with_U)" class="mw-redirect" title="Run Away (I Wanna Be with U)">Run Away (I Wanna Be with U)</a>", respectively, thanks to his relationship with The Neptunes, who produced both songs.
</p><p>In early 2001, Pharrell Williams signed the duo to <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a> through his recently established <a href="/wiki/Star_Trak_Entertainment" title="Star Trak Entertainment">Star Trak</a> imprint. Clipse began working on their major label debut, executively produced by The Neptunes. Their debut single, <i><a href="/wiki/Grindin%27" title="Grindin&#39;">Grindin'</a></i> was released on May 14, 2002, and became a summer Top 40 hit, reaching number 30 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> on July 30, 2002. Similar success followed with their second single, <i><a href="/wiki/When_the_Last_Time" title="When the Last Time">When the Last Time</a></i>, which peaked at #19. Fueled by two successful singles, Clipse released their commercial debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Lord_Willin%27" title="Lord Willin&#39;">Lord Willin'</a></i> on August 20, 2002, debuting at #1 on Billboard's Top R&amp;B/Hip-hop Album chart and #4 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">Billboard 200</a>, eventually being certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) on October 1, 2002.
</p><p>In late 2003, Clipse began recording material for their second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hell_Hath_No_Fury_(Clipse_album)" title="Hell Hath No Fury (Clipse album)">Hell Hath No Fury</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> However, further work on the album ground to a halt in 2004, when <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista Records</a>'s urban artists were absorbed into its sister label <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> as part of a larger merger between <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Music_Group" title="Bertelsmann Music Group">BMG</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Due to contractual requirements, Clipse was forced to stay on Jive, while Star Trak and the rest of its roster moved to their new home at <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> While Clipse resumed work on the album, and eventually finished recording it, the duo became increasingly frustrated with Jive, as the label was notorious for overlooking various hip-hop/R&amp;B artists in favor of more pop-oriented acts on its roster. The label's musical strategy expansion caused numerous delays in the release of <i>Hell Hath No Fury</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As delays continued, the group asked for a formal release from its contract. When Jive refused to grant this request, the duo sued the label.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In response to this, in 2004, the brothers launched their own record label imprint, Re-Up Records, and formed the hip hop group <a href="/wiki/Re-Up_Gang" title="Re-Up Gang">Re-Up Gang</a>, along with fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/Ab-Liva" class="mw-redirect" title="Ab-Liva">Ab-Liva</a> and Sandman.
</p><p>
On May 9, 2006, Clipse finally reached an agreement with Jive to release the album through both Re-Up and Jive.<sup id="cite_ref-Reference_2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <i>Hell Hath No Fury</i> was finally released on November 28, 2006. Once again produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, it debuted at #14 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with over 80,000 copies sold in the 1st week. While the album received a great deal of critical acclaim, its sales were less successful than Lord Willin'.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It spawned two moderately successful singles: "<a href="/wiki/Mr._Me_Too" title="Mr. Me Too">Mr. Me Too</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Wamp_Wamp_(What_It_Do)" title="Wamp Wamp (What It Do)">Wamp Wamp (What It Do)</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Slim_Thug" title="Slim Thug">Slim Thug</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Clipse's frustrations with Jive were a constant theme of the album, with Pusha T saying <i>"I'm sorry to the fans, but them crackers weren't playing fair at Jive"</i> on the track <i>Mr. Me Too</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> magazine <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="XXL magazine">XXL</a></i> gave the album a "XXL" rating, marking it as a five-star album. At the time only five albums had previously received that honor.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>  </p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pusha_T.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pusha_T.jpg/170px-Pusha_T.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pusha_T.jpg/255px-Pusha_T.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pusha_T.jpg/340px-Pusha_T.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a><figcaption>Pusha T performing at the 2007&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Music_Festival" title="Pitchfork Music Festival"><i>Pitchfork</i> Music Festival</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In a May 19, 2007, interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Eye_Weekly" title="Eye Weekly">Eye Weekly</a></i>, Clipse revealed that they had been officially released from any contractual obligations with Jive.<sup id="cite_ref-Reference_3_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_3-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> After this, the duo began discussions with several record labels, eventually signing with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> on October 26, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Reference_5_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_5-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The follow-up to <i>Hell Hath No Fury</i>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Til_the_Casket_Drops_(Clipse_album)" title="Til the Casket Drops (Clipse album)">Til the Casket Drops</a></i>, was released on December 8, 2009, via Columbia Records.<sup id="cite_ref-Release_Date_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Release_Date-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In a departure from the group's previous works, which only featured production from the Neptunes, the album features production from <a href="/wiki/Sean_%22Diddy%22_Combs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean &quot;Diddy&quot; Combs">Sean "Diddy" Combs</a>' production team <a href="/wiki/The_Hitmen_(production_team)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hitmen (production team)">The Hitmen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khalil" title="DJ Khalil">DJ Khalil</a> among others. The album did not fare as well commercially as the group's first two albums, peaking at only #41 on the Billboard 200.<sup id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932011:_Solo_career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2011:_Solo_career_beginnings">2010–2011: Solo career beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2010–2011: Solo career beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After releasing their third album, Pusha T and Malice announced Clipse would be going on indefinite hiatus so the brothers could focus on their solo careers. Shortly after this, Pusha T was signed to <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> label in September 2010, and made his first appearance as a member of the GOOD roster on Kanye West's <i><a href="/wiki/My_Beautiful_Dark_Twisted_Fantasy" title="My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy">My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy</a></i>, appearing on his hit "<a href="/wiki/Runaway_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Runaway (Kanye West song)">Runaway</a>" and premiering the song with him at the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a> on September 12, 2010. He was also featured on several tracks from West's <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Fridays" title="GOOD Fridays">GOOD Fridays</a> series and made other appearances on <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>'s Monster Mondays series, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/H.F.M._2_(Hunger_for_More_2)" class="mw-redirect" title="H.F.M. 2 (Hunger for More 2)">H.F.M. 2 (Hunger for More 2)</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Tabi_Bonney" title="Tabi Bonney">Tabi Bonney</a>'s <i>Fresh</i>, respectively. On the week of December 16, 2010, Pusha T signed an exclusive management deal with <a href="/wiki/NUE_Agency" title="NUE Agency">NUE Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On February 11, 2011, <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a> debuted Pusha T's debut solo single on <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The track, titled "My God", was produced by <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a> and was generally well received by the public. Soon after, the song leaked onto the internet, however was not officially released through iTunes and Amazon until August 24, 2011. On August 31, 2011, it was announced Pusha had signed a solo record deal with <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam">Def Jam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 21, 2011, Pusha T released his solo debut, a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> titled <i>Fear of God</i>, which included "My God" and featured both <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyles</a> and original songs, and included features from Kanye West, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rick Ross (rapper)">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Cossom" title="Kevin Cossom">Kevin Cossom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was well received, and soon after he began working on his debut <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a> (EP) <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_of_God_II:_Let_Us_Pray" title="Fear of God II: Let Us Pray">Fear of God II: Let Us Pray</a></i>, which initially included four songs from the mixtape and five new songs. The EP was originally set to be released on June 21, 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-mtv_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> however, it was pushed back to August 23, and for a while September 27 was believed to be the date, but after it came and went, on October 6, 2011, Pusha T announced the EP was set to be released on November 8, 2011. In addition, it was revealed he had added four more songs to the EP, bringing it to 12 tracks in total.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  Considered a re-release of the initial <i>Fear of God</i>, it was released on November 8, 2011, and was well received by critics.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Christgau_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg/220px-Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg/330px-Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg/440px-Kanye_at_Lollapalooza_Santiago_2011_9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="898" data-file-height="681" /></a><figcaption>Pusha T (left) performing "<a href="/wiki/Runaway_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Runaway (Kanye West song)">Runaway</a>" with Kanye West at <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza_Chile" title="Lollapalooza Chile">Lollapalooza Chile</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>The first single from <i>Fear of God II: Let Us Pray</i> was leaked onto the Internet on July 8, 2011. The song, titled "<a href="/wiki/Trouble_on_My_Mind" title="Trouble on My Mind">Trouble on My Mind</a>", features <a href="/wiki/Odd_Future" title="Odd Future">Odd Future</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_The_Creator" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyler, The Creator">Tyler, The Creator</a>. The EP's second single, "Amen", was released September 13, 2011. The song, originally meant for <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>, was produced by <a href="/wiki/Shawty_Redd" title="Shawty Redd">Shawty Redd</a> and features verses from Kanye West and Young Jeezy, respectively. After the EP's release on November 8, the project debuted at number 66 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with 8,900 copies sold in its first week released.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> It also entered at number ten on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a>, at number eight on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Top_Rap_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Rap Albums">Top Rap Albums</a>, and at number 25 on its <a href="/wiki/Top_Digital_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Digital Albums">Digital Albums</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;B_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;B-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rap_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rap-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, Pusha T appeared on the second season of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> <a href="/wiki/Serial_(radio_and_television)" title="Serial (radio and television)">series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Make_It_in_America" title="How to Make It in America">How to Make It in America</a></i>. He played the role of a henchman for Urban Caribbean League.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> After the release of his EP, Pusha T started working on his solo debut studio album, which would be executively produced by Kanye West.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Pusha also said that after the release of his solo debut album and the <a href="/wiki/Re-Up_Gang" title="Re-Up Gang">Re-Up Gang</a> mixtape, <i>Long Live the Cane</i>, <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a> would also reunite and release another album.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In late 2011, Pusha made a guest appearance on English pop music|pop singer <a href="/wiki/Pixie_Lott" title="Pixie Lott">Pixie Lott</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/What_Do_You_Take_Me_For%3F" title="What Do You Take Me For?">What Do You Take Me For?</a>", the second single from her second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Young_Foolish_Happy" title="Young Foolish Happy">Young Foolish Happy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The song was a <a href="/wiki/Hit_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Hit single">hit single</a> in the UK, peaking at number ten on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Top_40" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Top 40">UK Top 40</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932014:_My_Name_Is_My_Name"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2014:_My_Name_Is_My_Name">2012–2014: <i>My Name Is My Name</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2012–2014: My Name Is My Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is_My_Name" title="My Name Is My Name">My Name Is My Name</a></div>
<p>On October 19, 2011, via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, Kanye West announced plans for a Spring 2012 <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> album, featuring all artists from the label as well as numerous guest appearances. On April 6, 2012, "<a href="/wiki/Mercy_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Mercy (Kanye West song)">Mercy</a>", the lead single from the GOOD Music compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Cruel_Summer_(GOOD_Music_album)" title="Cruel Summer (GOOD Music album)">Cruel Summer</a></i> was released. The song, produced by newly signed in-house producer Lifted, features Pusha T along with Kanye West, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">southern rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On May 24, 2012, Pusha T released a song titled "Exodus 23:1" featuring <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>. It is speculated that the song is a <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss track</a> aimed at <a href="/wiki/Young_Money" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Money">Young Money</a> rappers <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-youngmoney_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngmoney-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in a diss-song by Lil Wayne, which Pusha T did not directly respond to, but branded it as "horrible" in an interview.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He was featured alongside West on the third single for <i>Cruel Summer</i> - "<a href="/wiki/New_God_Flow" title="New God Flow">New God Flow</a>". In October 2012, Pusha T made an appearance on the <a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Iron_Fists_(soundtrack)" title="The Man with the Iron Fists (soundtrack)">soundtrack to the film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Iron_Fists" title="The Man with the Iron Fists">The Man with the Iron Fists</a></i> on a track titled "Tick Tock" alongside fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joell_Ortiz" title="Joell Ortiz">Joell Ortiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brown_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Danny Brown (rapper)">Danny Brown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 8, 2012, Pusha T released "<a href="/wiki/Pain_(Pusha_T_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pain (Pusha T song)">Pain</a>" featuring southern rapper <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, the first single from his debut album. That same day <a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)"><i>Spin</i> magazine</a> reported that Pusha T's debut album had been pushed back until 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> While performing in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Canada, it was reported that Pusha T announced he would be releasing a mixtape entitled <i>Wrath of Caine</i> preceding the release of his debut studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-www.hiphopdx.com_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.hiphopdx.com-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Later in November, Thornton announced the title of his debut studio album to be <i><a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is_My_Name" title="My Name Is My Name">My Name Is My Name</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On December 5, 2012, Pusha T released "Blocka" the first single from his <i>Wrath of Caine</i> mixtape. The song features <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Popcaan" title="Popcaan">Popcaan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The music video for the song was released on December 11, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was released on January 28, 2013, along with the announcement of his album coming at the end of the first quarter of 2013. In January 2013 it was announced that Pusha would be performing at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pusha_T_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Pusha_T_2013.jpg/170px-Pusha_T_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="222" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Pusha_T_2013.jpg/255px-Pusha_T_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Pusha_T_2013.jpg/340px-Pusha_T_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1903" data-file-height="2484" /></a><figcaption>Pusha T performing in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p><i>My Name Is My Name</i> was scheduled to be released on July 16, 2013, but was pushed back to October. Pusha T's debut studio album was released on October 8, 2013, featuring guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>, <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, among others. The album was met with acclaim from music critics and was positioned high on many "Best Albums of 2013" lists by major publications. The album also fared well commercially, debuting at number 4 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 74,000 copies in its first week of release. As of July 8, 2017, the album has sold 182,000 copies in the United States. The album was promoted by five singles: "<a href="/wiki/Pain_(Pusha_T_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pain (Pusha T song)">Pain</a>" featuring Future, "Numbers on the Boards", "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Serenade" title="Sweet Serenade">Sweet Serenade</a>" featuring Chris Brown, "Let Me Love You" featuring <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Nosetalgia" title="Nosetalgia">Nosetalgia</a>" featuring Kendrick Lamar, along with the promotional single "Who I Am" featuring 2 Chainz and Big Sean.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The album includes production from Kanye West, <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a>, <a href="/wiki/No_I.D." title="No I.D.">No I.D.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottz" title="Nottz">Nottz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Cannon" title="Don Cannon">Don Cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, among others. In an April 2013 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/AskMen" title="AskMen">AskMen</a></i>, Pusha revealed that shortly after his debut album was released, he would finish working on his second album, titled <i>King Push</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-SecondLP_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SecondLP-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Pusha T provided guest vocals over a Vice remix of "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_Gone_(Linkin_Park_song)" title="I&#39;ll Be Gone (Linkin Park song)">I'll Be Gone</a>" for the remix album, <i><a href="/wiki/Recharged_(Linkin_Park_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Recharged (Linkin Park album)">Recharged</a></i>, by American rock band <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932018:_King_Push_.E2.80.93_Darkest_Before_Dawn"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2018:_King_Push_–_Darkest_Before_Dawn">2014–2018: <i>King Push – Darkest Before Dawn</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014–2018: King Push – Darkest Before Dawn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/King_Push_%E2%80%93_Darkest_Before_Dawn:_The_Prelude" title="King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude">King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude</a></div>
<p>On November 19, 2014, Pusha released a single titled "<a href="/wiki/Lunch_Money_(song)" title="Lunch Money (song)">Lunch Money</a>", produced by Kanye West.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, Pusha T <i>King Push</i> for a Spring 2015 release.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In May 2015, he announced the album would be pushed back to June.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On November 9, 2015, Pusha revealed to <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> that he had been appointed the new president of GOOD Music.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pusha_T_(21898809281).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg/170px-Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg/255px-Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg/340px-Pusha_T_%2821898809281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1994" data-file-height="2656" /></a><figcaption>Pusha T performing at the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Hopscotch_Music_Festival" title="Hopscotch Music Festival">Hopscotch Music Festival</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>On November 12, 2015, Pusha T released a single titled "Untouchable", produced by <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On November 23, 2015, it was announced that Pusha T would release a new album, <i><a href="/wiki/King_Push_%E2%80%93_Darkest_Before_Dawn:_The_Prelude" title="King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude">King Push – Darkest Before Dawn: The Prelude</a></i> before the aforementioned <i>King Push</i> album, serving as a prelude to <i>King Push</i>. It was released on December 18, 2015, and received widespread acclaim from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-metacritic_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <i>Darkest Before Dawn</i> reached over 17 million streams in its first week. On May 31, 2016, Pusha T released the lead single from his upcoming <i>King Push</i> album, <i><a href="/wiki/Drug_Dealers_Anonymous" title="Drug Dealers Anonymous">Drug Dealers Anonymous</a></i> featuring <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>, initially exclusively through Jay Z's streaming service <a href="/wiki/Tidal_(service)" title="Tidal (service)">Tidal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a June 2016 interview, former record executive <a href="/wiki/Steve_Stoute" title="Steve Stoute">Steve Stoute</a> claimed that Pusha T had allegedly written the <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s_advertising" title="McDonald&#39;s advertising">McDonald's "I'm lovin' it" jingle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Thornton later confirmed the news on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> However, this claim has been disputed by advertising executives who created the campaign, and a McDonald's marketing executive. Neither Stoute nor Pusha T have commented on the dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, he collaborated once again with Linkin Park on the song "<a href="/wiki/Good_Goodbye" title="Good Goodbye">Good Goodbye</a>" of the band's seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/One_More_Light" title="One More Light">One More Light</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In the same year, Pusha T collaborated with the virtual band <a href="/wiki/Gorillaz" title="Gorillaz">Gorillaz</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Out_(song)" title="Let Me Out (song)">Let Me Out</a>" from their studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Humanz" title="Humanz">Humanz</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.932022:_Daytona_and_It.27s_Almost_Dry"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2022:_Daytona_and_It's_Almost_Dry">2018–2022: <i>Daytona</i> and <i>It's Almost Dry</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2018–2022: Daytona and It&#039;s Almost Dry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Daytona_(album)" title="Daytona (album)">Daytona (album)</a> and <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Almost_Dry" title="It&#39;s Almost Dry">It's Almost Dry</a></div>
<p>On April 19, 2018, Kanye West announced on his Twitter page that Pusha T's <i>King Push</i> album would be released on May 25, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On May 23, 2018, Pusha T announced on his Twitter page that he changed the album title from <i>King Push</i> to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_(album)" title="Daytona (album)"><i>Daytona</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The album garnered controversy when West spent $85,000 to acquire the cover art: a photo of <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>'s drug-filled bathroom, taken in her <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta, Georgia</a> residence in 2006. Not only did the content of the album cover cause outside controversy, but Pusha T claims to not have agreed with the price West paid for the photo.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  On May 25, 2018, <i>Daytona</i> released to critical acclaim. It received an 86 on Metacritic, indicating "universal acclaim".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, he was named the "Best Rapper Alive" by <a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a> for 2018 for his work on <i>Daytona</i> and his diss track "<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Adidon" title="The Story of Adidon">The Story of Adidon</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The album received praise from hip-hop veterans Nas and P. Diddy, calling it "a classic album" and "a modern day masterpiece".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2020, Pusha T started a new record label, Heir Wave Media Group, to sign and develop artists from the <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> area. He remained the president of <a href="/wiki/G.O.O.D._Music" class="mw-redirect" title="G.O.O.D. Music">G.O.O.D. Music</a> while focusing on building a roster of artists from his home state. In creating the label, Pusha cited his desire to recruit "album artists" who craft narratives and larger stories throughout their projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Local artists were encouraged to submit music to the Heir Wave Music YouTube channel and a weekly radio show on a local station, <a href="/wiki/WOWI" title="WOWI">103 Jamz FM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pilot_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pilot-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the label's first year, Heir Wave Music signed Kahri 1k, Shaolinn, Leeto, and WhyNotDuce.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DMVRevamped_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DMVRevamped-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 7, 2022, Pusha T released "<a href="/wiki/Diet_Coke_(song)" title="Diet Coke (song)">Diet Coke</a>", the lead single from his fourth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Almost_Dry" title="It&#39;s Almost Dry">It's Almost Dry</a></i>, which was produced by Kanye West and <a href="/wiki/88-Keys" title="88-Keys">88-Keys</a>. The music video for the single was released the next day, directed by Omar Jones, and features Pusha T and West moving around over a white backdrop, which pays direct homage to <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mack" title="Craig Mack">Craig Mack</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Flava_in_Ya_Ear" title="Flava in Ya Ear">Flava in Ya Ear (Remix)</a>" music video.<sup id="cite_ref-Okayplayer_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okayplayer-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> 88-Keys later revealed that the beat for the single was made 18 years before the song was made, on a beat tape named <i>The Makings of Crack Cocaine</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HipHopDX_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HipHopDX-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 4, Pusha T and <a href="/wiki/Nigo" title="Nigo">Nigo</a> released the single "Hear Me Clearly" for Nigo's album <i><a href="/wiki/I_Know_Nigo!" title="I Know Nigo!">I Know Nigo!</a></i>, the song is also set to appear on <i>It's Almost Dry</i>. He also appeared alongside his brother No Malice as Clipse on the song "Punch Bowl" on the <i>I Know Nigo!</i> album as well. The music video also for "Hear Me Clearly" released on March 30.<sup id="cite_ref-Hypebeast_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hypebeast-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On that same month on the 21st, Pusha T appeared in a commercial for fast food chain <a href="/wiki/Arby%27s" title="Arby&#39;s">Arby's</a>, with a diss track named "Spicy Fish Diss" aimed at fellow fast food chain <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> because of their Fillet-O-Fish sandwich, and states that Arby's' Fish Sandwich is better.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> This was revenge toward the company for not crediting him for helping popularize the "I'm lovin' it" advertising campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 6, Pusha T released the third single for <i>It's Almost Dry</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Neck_%26_Wrist" title="Neck &amp; Wrist">Neck &amp; Wrist</a>" featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and Pharrell, and would later appear in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Charlamagne_tha_God" title="Charlamagne tha God">Charlamagne tha God</a>, which released on the 11th.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On the 18th, Pusha T announced the release date of <i>It's Almost Dry</i> as April 22,<sup id="cite_ref-Billboardb_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboardb-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and also announced a listening party in New York City named "Cokechella".<sup id="cite_ref-Fader_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The long-awaited album, primarily produced by frequent collaborators <a href="/wiki/Pharrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharrell">Pharrell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Ye</a>, was released on April 22 to widespread critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On the week dated May 7, 2022, it debuted atop the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">Billboard 200</a> with a total of 55,000 album equivalent units, becoming Pusha T's first number-one album on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2022-present:_Heir_Wave_Music_Group_and_departure_from_GOOD_Music">2022-present: Heir Wave Music Group and departure from GOOD Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2022-present: Heir Wave Music Group and departure from GOOD Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2022, Pusha T announced his departure from GOOD Music after founder Kanye West's <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitic</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Lives_Matter" title="White Lives Matter">pro-race</a> remarks. Speaking on West's support for "White Lives Matter", his <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West_2024_presidential_campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanye West 2024 presidential campaign">2024 presidential campaign</a> and other public outbursts, Pusha T stated that they were nothing to "tap dance around".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> His departure also ended his tenure as the label's president. Shortly after, he changed his focus on his own label, the Heir Wave Music Group.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Pusha T performed at the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_2023" title="Coachella 2023">22nd Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a> in April 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feuds">Feuds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Feuds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequence">Consequence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Consequence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Pusha T released "My God", the first single from his solo mixtape, his former <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> label-mate <a href="/wiki/Consequence_(rapper)" title="Consequence (rapper)">Consequence</a> took to <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and claimed Pusha T stole his flow and lyrics from a song of his that Pusha T was supposed to appear on, titled "The Last Supper".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On July 22, 2011, Consequence released a song titled "The Plagiarist Society" where he takes shots and questions Pusha T's <a href="/wiki/Mafioso_rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Mafioso rap">coke-dealing raps</a>. Towards the end of the record, the Queens native promises to take aim at Kanye West next saying "You're nothing but a body shield, for that coward from the mid-west/ so yes you can bet, that your boss is next".
</p><p>Pusha T responded to the diss track when he appeared on <a href="/wiki/WGCI-FM" title="WGCI-FM">Chicago's 107.5 WGCI's The Morning Riot</a> and said nobody is looking for Consequence, as for if he would respond on a record, Pusha T went on to say "At the end of the day I am an artist and this whole rap thing is fun to me, so I can't say you won't hear nothing, but to go back and forth with him, it's not right, I won't get anything out of it."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Later that day, Consequence called into Chicago's WGCI's The Morning Riot in retaliation to the remarks Pusha T made about him. He also premiered a song titled "Everybody Told Me 2 (Straighten It Out)" where he disses West, Pusha T and GOOD Music in general.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Since then Pusha T has responded to Consequence on a record. The song was the remix to <a href="/wiki/Ace_Hood" title="Ace Hood">Ace Hood</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Go_%27N%27_Get_It" class="mw-redirect" title="Go &#39;N&#39; Get It">Go 'N' Get It</a>" which also featured <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Sigel" title="Beanie Sigel">Beanie Sigel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Styles_P" title="Styles P">Styles P</a>. In the song Pusha raps "Consequence, nigga, talk is cheap You don't want a problem? Off the beef Before I off his ass with his awful teeth". On August 19, Consequence released <i>Movies on Demand 3</i> and continued to <a href="/wiki/Diss_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Diss track">diss</a> his former label and Pusha T on songs such as "Career Killer" and "Mr.RapFix (Hot Water)".
</p><p>On September 15, 2011, Consequence appeared on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s Rap Fix and announced his feud with Kanye West and GOOD Music was over.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> While out in Chicago in October 2011, Pusha T appeared on WGCI radio for a second time, and confirmed that the "beef" was indeed over, that it had died out and they have moved on. In January 2015, the two officially ended the feud when Consequence took to his Instagram page to let the people know: "All G.O.O.D. in 2015, Pusha [T] and I deaded everything and we creatively vibed with Kanye for this <a href="/wiki/The_Life_of_Pablo" title="The Life of Pablo">new LP</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lil_Wayne">Lil Wayne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Lil Wayne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The tension between Pusha T and rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> had been going on for years, beginning soon after <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Birdman (entertainer)">Birdman</a> worked on "What Happened to That Boy", the latter's 2002 single. In 2006, Wayne felt the Clipse song "<a href="/wiki/Mr._Me_Too" title="Mr. Me Too">Mr. Me Too</a>" was directed at him,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and in 2012 Pusha T's "Exodus 23:1" song caused Lil Wayne to vent on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, later releasing a diss track titled "Goulish", in which he says "Fuck Pusha T and anybody that love him / His head up his ass, I'mma have to head-butt him".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Pusha T has called Wayne's diss track "horrible" and said he felt it did not deserve a response. Both men have downplayed the feud, with Wayne saying he is over it.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> However, in September 2012, Pusha T appeared on the remix of <a href="/wiki/Chief_Keef" title="Chief Keef">Chief Keef</a>'s <a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Like" title="I Don&#39;t Like">I Don't Like</a>, where he accused Wayne of using <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwriters</a> saying, "My pen's better, you don't write, trendsetter, you clone-like", he has since confirmed that the line was a Wayne diss.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In late November 2012, Pusha T once again dissed Wayne and <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a> song titled "Mad Fo" from his <i>#IDGAF</i> mixtape. Pusha T later revealed his motivation for the verse: "Oh because it's a <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz</a> beat. You got to blame Swizz. See, when Wayne got a Swizz beat... with the "Ghoulish" track; he got busy, well he tried to."<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drake">Drake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Drake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Adidon" title="The Story of Adidon">The Story of Adidon</a></div>
<p>After the release of Pusha T's song "Exodus 23:1" in 2012, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a> seemingly responded to Pusha on the intro to his 2013 album <i><a href="/wiki/Nothing_Was_the_Same" title="Nothing Was the Same">Nothing Was the Same</a></i>, calling Pusha T a "bench player acting like a starter". The two directed subliminal disses towards each other between 2012 and 2017 with Pusha T rapping on the song "H.G.T.V", "It's too far gone when the realest ain't real / I walk amongst the clouds, so your ceilings ain't real/ These niggas Call of Duty 'cause they killings ain't real / With a questionable pen so the feeling ain't real,"<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> with Drake later responding on the diss track "<a href="/wiki/Two_Birds,_One_Stone" title="Two Birds, One Stone">Two Birds, One Stone</a>" questioning Pusha T's drug dealing past.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pusha T further escalated the feud on the song "Infrared" from his 2018 album <i><a href="/wiki/Daytona_(album)" title="Daytona (album)">Daytona</a></i>, where he accused Drake of using a <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwriter</a>. Drake responded to the song less than one day later, releasing a track titled "<a href="/wiki/Duppy_Freestyle" title="Duppy Freestyle">Duppy Freestyle</a>" where he insults both Pusha T and <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, accusing Pusha of being a fake drug dealer and claiming that he would boost sales of Pusha T's album just by dissing him.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Pusha T responded to Duppy on May 29, 2018, with the track "<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Adidon" title="The Story of Adidon">The Story of Adidon</a>" which featured Pusha responding to Drake over the instrumental of Jay-Z's 2017 single "<a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_O.J." title="The Story of O.J.">The Story of O.J</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The song debuted on Hot 97 and has lines directed towards rumors Drake has an illegitimate child<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/40_(record_producer)" title="40 (record producer)">his producer</a>'s multiple sclerosis.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The song additionally referenced Pusha's ongoing beef with Lil Wayne and Birdman.  The song's cover art also attracted controversy, showing an unedited picture of Drake wearing a <a href="/wiki/Jim_Crow" class="mw-redirect" title="Jim Crow">Jim Crow</a> t-shirt and hoodie and <a href="/wiki/Blackface" title="Blackface">blackface</a> makeup.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Drake eventually admitted to losing the feud in an interview with RapRadar, saying it was his "first loss in the competitive sport of rapping."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pusha_T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On June 11, 2020, Pusha T and&#160;his wife Virginia Williams welcomed their first child, Nigel Brixx Thornton.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The child's name attracted reactions online for "Brixx" being an apparent slang term for cocaine, something which Pusha T raps about often.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2021, Pusha T's mother died<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> as did his father four months later.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
